     8	
     9	## Summary
    10	
    11	Four small runner improvements that reduce operator friction:
    12	
    13	1. **Raise default character budgets** (plan Fix 7) — current defaults force partial-coverage retries on normal-sized specs. Raise to `--max-artifact-chars 40000`, `--max-context-chars 50000`, `--max-total-chars 200000`.
    14	2. **`checkpoint --validation-only`** (plan Fix 5) — past the 3-round adversarial cap, an operator editing an artifact to address judge-flagged issues has no CLI path to re-seal the manifest without dispatching expensive reviews. Add a no-review validation-only mode that just re-verifies the manifest against the current artifact SHA.
    15	3. **Restatement judge gameability** (PR #744 adversarial P2-6) — the current "diminishing returns" rule counts severity transitions. A bad-faith operator could file HIGH findings in round 1 and downgrade to MEDIUM in round 2 to trigger proceed. Harden the prompt to require quoting prior-round reasoning text when citing severity drop.
    16	4. **Discover CLI append semantics** (PR #744 + PR #749 postmortems) — passing `--non-goal X --non-goal Y` in one invocation currently keeps only `Y`. Change to append semantics; add explicit `--clear-non-goals` / `--clear-acceptance-criteria` flags for destructive cases.
    17	
    18	All four land in the runner's existing modules. Together they remove four distinct friction points that operators have actually hit (the last two showed up in this very feature's own discovery phase).
    19	
    20	## Problem statement
    21	
    22	### Fix 1 — Char budget churn
    23	
    24	[factory_review_specs.py](../../operations/codex-skills/feature-factory/scripts/factory_review_specs.py) and related modules default to conservative character budgets. During both PR #744 and PR #749 runs, the operator had to pass explicit `--max-artifact-chars 50000 --max-total-chars 250000` to avoid "artifact too large for partial coverage" failures on normal-sized specs. The defaults are set too low for real-world artifacts in this codebase.
    25	
    26	### Fix 2 — Re-seal after post-cap edits
    27	
    28	Once `adversarial_rounds >= 3`, further `checkpoint --stage X` runs are blocked by the cap — correctly, since we don't want to launch round 4 of adversarial review. But if the operator edits the artifact after the cap (to address a judge-flagged issue), there's no CLI path to re-sync the manifest SHA without bypassing the workflow. Today the operator hand-edits review frontmatter SHAs. We did that during PR #744 and #749 finalization. The correct answer is a `--validation-only` mode: skip review dispatch, just re-verify the manifest is consistent with the current artifact.
    29	
    30	### Fix 3 — Restatement judge severity-drop gaming
    31	
    32	PR #744's adversarial review raised this (finding P2-6). The restatement judge's "diminishing-returns" rule says: if prior rounds had HIGH and this round has only MEDIUM/LOW, proceed — the loop is converging. But a prompt-aware operator could:
    33	- Round 1: inject HIGH finding X with dubious justification
    34	- Round 2: reviewer mentions X but classifies it MEDIUM
    35	- Restatement judge: "severity dropped HIGH→MEDIUM, proceed"
    36	- Real HIGH issue ships undetected
    37	
    38	The fix is to make the severity-drop claim have *evidence*: the judge must quote prior-round reasoning text and name the specific finding whose severity allegedly dropped. That makes gaming much harder — to bypass, you'd need to create a fake round-1 HIGH that the judge can then quote as "now-dropped-to-MEDIUM" with text.
    39	
    40	### Fix 4 — Discover CLI silent-overwrite footgun
    41	
    42	Both PR #744 and PR #749's discovery phases hit the same footgun: passing multiple `--non-goal` or `--acceptance-criteria` flags in one invocation silently keeps only the last value. I scripted a for-loop workaround both times. The fix is append semantics by default, with explicit `--clear-non-goals` / `--clear-acceptance-criteria` flags for the rare destructive case.
    43	
    44	## Scope
    45	
    46	### In scope
    47	
    48	- **Fix 1** — raise default char budgets in `factory_cmd_checkpoint.py` argparse defaults for `--max-artifact-chars`, `--max-context-chars`, `--max-total-chars`.
    49	- **Fix 2** — add `--validation-only` flag to `checkpoint` subcommand. When set, skip reviewer dispatch entirely, just re-verify the manifest against the current artifact SHA. If drift, re-seal the manifest (updates stored SHAs to match current artifact). Exits 0 on success, 2 on error.
    50	- **Fix 3** — update `judge-prompts/restatement.md` to require quoting prior-round reasoning when citing severity drop.
    51	- **Fix 4** — in `factory_cmd_discover.py`, change `--non-goal` and `--acceptance-criteria` from `store` to `append` action. Add `--clear-non-goals` / `--clear-acceptance-criteria` flags.
    52	- **Tests** for all four behaviors.
    53	
    54	### Out of scope
    55	
    56	- Completeness judge veto (Feature A — shipped).
    57	- Auto-register mutating commands (Feature A — shipped).
    58	- Review intermediate GC (Feature A — shipped).
    59	- Embedding concern IDs (Feature C — deferred).
    60	- Rename `repair_X_checkpoint` (skipped).
    61	- `--force-advance` CLI (subsumed).
    62	- Structured JSON reviewer output (larger project).
    63	
    64	## User stories
    65	
    66	### US1 — Char budgets match real specs (Priority: P2)
    67	
    68	**As** the orchestrator running a checkpoint
    69	**I need** the default char budgets to match real-world spec sizes in this codebase
    70	**So that** I don't have to pass explicit `--max-*-chars` flags on every invocation.
    71	
    72	**Why P2**: quality of life, not correctness. Operators who know the flags can already opt out. But the defaults cause first-time-user friction and retry churn.
    73	
    74	**Independent test**: invoke `checkpoint --stage spec` with no `--max-*-chars` flags against a fixture with a 30k-char spec. Assert no partial-coverage warning. Assert the 3 values stored in the checkpoint manifest are the new defaults.
    75	
    76	**Acceptance scenarios**:
    77	
    78	1. **Given** a spec.md of 35k chars, **when** `checkpoint --stage spec` runs with no budget flags, **then** no partial-coverage retry happens.
    79	2. **Given** an operator explicitly passes `--max-artifact-chars 10000`, **when** checkpoint runs, **then** the operator's value wins (defaults don't override explicit flags).
    80	
    81	### US2 — Re-seal after post-cap edits (Priority: P1)
    82	
    83	**As** the orchestrator dealing with judge-flagged issues past the 3-round cap
    84	**I need** a `checkpoint --validation-only` mode that re-verifies the manifest without re-dispatching reviewers
    85	**So that** I can re-sync after an edit without burning agent calls or hand-editing review frontmatter SHAs.
    86	
    87	**Why P1**: this is the fix for a friction class that hit both PR #744 and PR #749 during their own runs. Hand-editing review frontmatter SHAs is exactly the kind of workflow bypass that Fix 1 in PR #744 was trying to eliminate.
    88	
    89	**Independent test**: produce a stage state with 3 adversarial rounds complete + an edited artifact (SHA drifted from manifest). Run `checkpoint --stage spec --validation-only`. Assert no subprocess calls to Codex or Gemini. Assert manifest + review frontmatter SHAs are updated to match current artifact. Exit 0.
    90	
    91	**Acceptance scenarios**:
    92	
    93	1. **Given** `adversarial_rounds == 3` and artifact SHA drifted from manifest, **when** `checkpoint --stage spec --validation-only` runs, **then** no reviewer is dispatched, manifest and review SHAs are updated, exit code is 0.
    94	2. **Given** same state but `--validation-only` is NOT passed, **when** checkpoint runs, **then** behavior is unchanged (blocked by 3-round cap or triggers repair path, whichever applies today).
    95	3. **Given** the artifact SHA matches the manifest already (no drift), **when** `--validation-only` runs, **then** exit 0, no-op, zero writes to review files.
    96	4. **Given** manifest file doesn't exist, **when** `--validation-only` runs, **then** exit 2 with "no manifest to validate".
    97	
    98	### US3 — Restatement judge severity-drop requires evidence (Priority: P2)
    99	
   100	**As** an operator trusting the judge panel
   101	**I need** the restatement judge to only proceed on severity-drop when it can quote specific prior-round reasoning
   102	**So that** the "diminishing returns" rule can't be gamed by injecting fake HIGH findings early.
   103	
   104	**Why P2**: low-probability attack, but the mitigation is almost free (prompt text change). Hardens a known soft spot from PR #744 adversarial review.
   105	
   106	**Independent test**: mock a restatement-judge call with verdict reasoning that cites severity drop but does NOT quote any prior-round text. Assert the judge schema validation fails the verdict (or the reasoning is flagged as non-conforming — the exact enforcement mechanism is prompt-level).
   107	
   108	**Acceptance scenarios**:
   109	
   110	1. **Given** the restatement-judge prompt is updated, **when** a judge run cites severity drop, **then** its reasoning contains at least one quoted block from a prior-round reviewer finding or prior-round judge verdict.
   111	2. **Given** the prompt change does not alter the first-round-proceed-with-annotation rule from PR #744, **when** running judge round 1 (no prior rounds), **then** verdict remains `proceed-with-annotation`.
   112	3. **Given** the prompt change does not alter the true-saturation rule, **when** 70%+ of latest findings are literal restatements, **then** verdict remains `proceed`.
   113	
   114	### US4 — Discover CLI accepts multiple values (Priority: P2)
   115	
   116	**As** an operator or an agent running discovery
   117	**I need** `discover --non-goal X --non-goal Y --non-goal Z` in one invocation to store all three values
   118	**So that** I don't have to script a for-loop or remember to pass flags one at a time.
   119	
   120	**Why P2**: quality of life. Agents (including this feature's own orchestrator) repeatedly hit this — two consecutive features had to work around it. Fix is ~5 lines.
   121	
   122	**Independent test**: invoke `discover --non-goal X --non-goal Y --non-goal Z` on a fresh workflow. Assert `state.discovery.non_goals == ["X", "Y", "Z"]` (order preserved, all present).
   123	
   124	**Acceptance scenarios**:
   125	
   126	1. **Given** no prior non-goals, **when** `discover --non-goal A --non-goal B` runs, **then** `state.discovery.non_goals == ["A", "B"]`.
   127	2. **Given** existing non-goals `["A"]`, **when** `discover --non-goal B --non-goal C` runs, **then** `state.discovery.non_goals == ["A", "B", "C"]` (append semantics preserved).
   128	3. **Given** existing non-goals `["A", "B", "C"]`, **when** `discover --clear-non-goals` runs, **then** `state.discovery.non_goals == []`.
   129	4. **Given** `discover --clear-non-goals --non-goal D` in one invocation, **when** it runs, **then** `state.discovery.non_goals == ["D"]` (clear happens first, then append).
   130	5. **Same semantics** for `--acceptance-criteria` / `--clear-acceptance-criteria`.
   131	
   132	## Functional requirements
   133	
   134	### Fix 1 — Raise default char budgets (US1)
   135	
   136	- **FR-001**: In `factory_cmd_checkpoint.py` argparse setup for the `checkpoint` subcommand, change defaults to `--max-artifact-chars 40000`, `--max-context-chars 50000`, `--max-total-chars 200000`.
   137	- **FR-002**: Operator-passed explicit values MUST still override the defaults (no change to precedence).
   138	- **FR-003**: Existing tests using smaller budgets MUST continue to pass (they pass explicit values, not defaults).
   139	
   140	### Fix 2 — `--validation-only` flag (US2)
   141	
   142	- **FR-004**: Add `--validation-only` to the `checkpoint` subcommand. Mutually exclusive with `--fallback` (reviewer replacement) — validation-only is purely a manifest-sync path.
   143	- **FR-005**: When `--validation-only` is set, `command_checkpoint` MUST:
   144	  - NOT dispatch any reviewer (no `codex exec`, no `gemini` subprocess).
   145	  - Load the stage's checkpoint manifest (`reviews/{stage}.checkpoint.json`).
   146	  - Compute the current artifact SHA via `workflow_utils.normalized_artifact_hash`.
   147	  - If SHAs match: print `manifest already matches artifact (sha={sha})`, exit 0.
   148	  - If SHAs differ: rewrite the manifest's `artifact_sha256` field AND update each referenced `.review.md` file's frontmatter `artifact_sha256` field to match. Print `manifest re-sealed from {old} to {new}`. Exit 0.
   149	  - If manifest doesn't exist: print `no manifest to validate — run checkpoint first`, exit 2.
   150	- **FR-006**: `--validation-only` MUST NOT bypass the lifecycle-concern gate from PR #749 — if prior-stage open concerns exist, deliver/next-checkpoint still blocks. This is a manifest-sync tool, not a workflow bypass.
   151	- **FR-007**: An annotation MUST be appended to `stages[stage].annotations[]` with type `"validation-only-reseal"` recording `{old_sha, new_sha, at: <epoch>}` when a reseal happens.
   152	
   153	### Fix 3 — Restatement judge severity-drop evidence (US3)
   154	
   155	- **FR-008**: Update `judge-prompts/restatement.md` to add a requirement under the diminishing-returns rule: "When citing severity drop as proceed justification, the verdict reasoning MUST quote at least one specific finding from prior rounds by its original reasoning text (first 60+ characters verbatim). If you cannot quote a prior round's text, severity-drop reasoning is not valid — vote based on other rules."
   156	- **FR-009**: The first-round-proceed-with-annotation rule from PR #744 MUST be preserved unchanged.
   157	- **FR-010**: The true-saturation rule (70%+ restatements → proceed) MUST be preserved unchanged.
   158	- **FR-011**: No schema change — the enforcement is prompt-level. A follow-up could add a structured `quoted_prior_finding: str` field, but this feature keeps scope minimal.
   159	
   160	### Fix 4 — Discover CLI append semantics (US4)
   161	
   162	- **FR-012**: In `factory_cmd_discover.py` argparse setup, change `--non-goal` and `--acceptance-criteria` from `action="store"` to `action="append"` (or equivalent — match existing codebase patterns). Each flag occurrence appends to an internal list.
   163	- **FR-013**: When `discover` runs, for each value in the appended list: add it to `state.discovery.non_goals` (or `acceptance_criteria`) if not already present (dedup by exact string match). Order preserved.
   164	- **FR-014**: Add new flags `--clear-non-goals` and `--clear-acceptance-criteria` (boolean). When set, the corresponding list is emptied BEFORE any append operations in the same invocation. This lets `discover --clear-non-goals --non-goal D` produce `["D"]`.
   165	- **FR-015**: No other discovery flags change behavior. `--assumption`, `--unresolved`, `--resolve`, `--defer`, `--answer`, `--question`, etc. keep their current semantics.
   166	
   167	### Shared
   168	
   169	- **FR-016**: All 183 existing runner tests MUST continue to pass. Target total: ~200.
   170	- **FR-017**: No change to CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, cloud/CLAUDE.md, cloud/AGENTS.md, MEMORY.md, .gitignore, or any file outside the scripts/judge-prompts directories.
   171	
   172	## Success criteria
   173	
   174	- **SC-001**: A fresh checkpoint invocation with no `--max-*-chars` flags uses 40k/50k/200k and doesn't trigger partial-coverage retry on a 35k-char spec.
   175	- **SC-002**: `checkpoint --stage spec --validation-only` on a drifted artifact re-seals the manifest + review frontmatter SHAs without any subprocess calls (verified via mock assertion).
   176	- **SC-003**: `--validation-only` on a matching-SHA artifact is a no-op.
   177	- **SC-004**: Restatement judge prompt contains the quote-evidence requirement; first-round + true-saturation rules preserved.
   178	- **SC-005**: `discover --non-goal A --non-goal B --non-goal C` in one invocation stores all 3 in order.
   179	- **SC-006**: `discover --clear-non-goals --non-goal D` produces `["D"]`.
   180	- **SC-007**: All 183 existing tests + 3 new test files green; target ~200 total.
   181	
   182	## Edge cases
   183	
   184	- **Char budgets**: if a spec is genuinely larger than 40k (rare), explicit `--max-artifact-chars` still works. No regression.
   185	- **`--validation-only` on first-ever checkpoint**: no manifest exists → exit 2 with clear message.
   186	- **`--validation-only` with `--fallback`**: mutually exclusive argparse error.
   187	- **`--validation-only` with `--address`/`--defer`/`--dismiss`**: those are concern-lifecycle flags; they're unchanged by this feature. If combined, the concern-lifecycle path runs (earlier in command_checkpoint) and `--validation-only` becomes a no-op.
   188	- **Restatement prompt rollback**: if a reviewer's output format drifts and can't be quoted, judge falls through to other rules — doesn't break.
   189	- **`discover` append + dedup**: `discover --non-goal A --non-goal A` once stores just `["A"]`, not `["A", "A"]`. Dedup is an explicit design choice per FR-013.
   190	
   191	## Assumptions carried in
   192	
   193	1. Scope is Fix 1+2+3+4 only — no scope creep.
   194	2. Char budget defaults 40k/50k/200k match actual observed spec/plan sizes in this codebase.
   195	3. `--validation-only` is a pure manifest-sync tool, not a workflow bypass — lifecycle gates still apply.
   196	4. Restatement judge severity-drop enforcement is prompt-level (no schema change). A structured field is a potential follow-up.
   197	5. Discover CLI uses argparse `action="append"` pattern, which matches existing Python idioms for repeated flags.
   198	6. Codex implements slices after spec/plan/tasks checkpoints healthy. Claude is orchestrator only.
   199	
   200	## Non-goals
   201	
   202	See discovery state — 7 deferred items.
   203	
   204	## Residual risks (with verification)
   205	
   206	- **Risk R1** — char budget raise causes unexpected OOM or rate-limit issues on very small hardware.
   207	  **verification:** existing tests mostly use explicit small budgets and are unaffected. Production runs against full-size specs can hit larger budgets anyway; defaults just prevent retry churn. If rate limits become an issue, operators can lower via flags.
   208	
   209	- **Risk R2** — `--validation-only` becomes a "quiet bypass" that operators use to skip reviews.
   210	  **verification:** doesn't skip the concern-lifecycle gate (FR-006). And the manifest-reseal annotation (FR-007) makes its use visible in the audit trail. Not a bypass, a sync tool.
   211	
   212	- **Risk R3** — restatement prompt gets overly strict and fails legitimate rounds.
   213	  **verification:** the quote rule is specifically scoped to severity-drop proceed justification. Other proceed paths (first-round, true-saturation) don't require quotes. If legitimate cases fail, they fall through to other rules.
   214	
   215	- **Risk R4** — append semantics break a caller that depended on overwrite behavior.
   216	  **verification:** nothing in the codebase relies on overwrite (confirmed by the fact that both feature runs before this one had to script for-loops to get append behavior). The explicit `--clear-*-goals` flags cover the intentional-destructive case.

   564	        diff_text = artifact_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
   565	        if len(diff_text) > HARD_DIFF_ARTIFACT_MAX_CHARS:

   599	        if args.json:
   600	            print(json.dumps(cap_hit_payload))
   601	        else:
   602	            print("→ next: judge_panel")
   603	        return 2
   604	
   605	    reviews_arg = getattr(args, "required_reviews", None)
   606	    if reviews_arg is None:
   607	        small_task_set = False
   608	        if args.stage in ("tasks", "closeout"):
   609	            # For "tasks": count from the artifact (tasks.md is the artifact).
   610	            # For "closeout": count from tasks.md in the workflow dir (artifact is closeout.md).

     1	# System Prompt
     2	You are a review-loop auditor.
     3	
     4	Your only job: determine whether the findings from the LATEST
     5	adversarial round are genuinely new issues, or whether they are
     6	restatements of themes already raised and addressed in earlier
     7	rounds.
     8	
     9	Review loops can go forever if each round produces cosmetic
    10	variations of already-handled concerns. Your output decides
    11	whether the loop is producing signal or noise.
    12	
    13	A finding is a RESTATEMENT if:
    14	- Earlier rounds raised the same underlying concern, AND
    15	- The orchestrator made a substantive change in response, AND
    16	- The new finding does not point at a new failure mode
    17	
    18	A finding is NEW if:
    19	- No earlier round raised this concern, OR
    20	- Earlier rounds raised it but the mitigation is now itself flawed
    21	  in a way the new finding surfaces
    22	
    23	## Verdict rules
    24	
    25	**First-round case (no prior findings exist):** You cannot assess
    26	restatement because there is nothing to compare against. Default
    27	to PROCEED-WITH-ANNOTATION in this case — the orchestrator needs
    28	signal from other judges (`completeness`, `implementation-risk`)
    29	to decide blocking, not from you. Note the findings you observed
    30	so later rounds have baseline to compare against.
    31	
    32	**Diminishing-returns case (prior rounds exist, latest findings
    33	are materially less severe than prior rounds):** PROCEED. Severity
    34	is ranked HIGH > MEDIUM > LOW. If prior rounds had HIGH findings
    35	and the latest round has only MEDIUM/LOW, the loop is converging.
    36	
    37	**True-saturation case (70%+ of latest findings are literal
    38	restatements of prior-round findings):** PROCEED.
    39	
    40	**Real-progress case (latest round surfaces genuinely new and
    41	material failure modes that were not covered before):** BLOCK.
    42	
    43	**Important non-blocking pattern:** a round that introduces new
    44	findings while prior findings remain addressed is NOT automatic
    45	block. Block only when the new findings point at load-bearing
    46	correctness or safety issues, not at cosmetic or belt-and-suspenders
    47	concerns.
    48	
    49	Be concrete. Quote specific text from both the old and new rounds
    50	when calling something a restatement.
    51	
    52	# User Prompt Template
    53	Earlier rounds' findings (with orchestrator responses):
    54	{prior_findings_and_fixes}
    55	
    56	Latest round's findings:
    57	{latest_findings}
    58	
    59	For each latest finding:
    60	1. Classify as NEW or RESTATEMENT
    61	2. If RESTATEMENT, quote the earlier finding it echoes and the
    62	   orchestrator response that addressed it
    63	3. If NEW, state the specific failure mode that was not previously
    64	   covered
    65	
    66	Then emit verdict JSON. Proceed = loop is saturated, block = loop
    67	is still finding real issues.

   144	def checkpoint_manifest(
   145	    slug: str,
   146	    stage: str,
   147	    artifact_path: Path,
   148	    base_ref: str | None,
   149	    extra_context: list[str],
   150	    reviews: list[dict[str, str]],
   151	    max_artifact_chars: int | None,
   152	    max_context_chars: int | None,
   153	    max_total_chars: int | None,
   154	    allow_dirty_paths: list[str] | None = None,
   155	) -> dict:
   156	    manifest_reviews = []
   157	    for spec in reviews:
   158	        output = reviews_dir(slug) / f"{stage}.{spec['reviewer']}.{spec['lens']}.review.md"
   159	        manifest_reviews.append(
   160	            {
   161	                "reviewer": spec["reviewer"],
   162	                "lens": spec["lens"],
   163	                "stage": stage,
   164	                "path": repo_relative_path(output, REPO_ROOT),
   165	                "context_paths": [repo_relative_path(resolve_stored_path(path, REPO_ROOT), REPO_ROOT) for path in extra_context],
   166	                **({"model": spec["model"]} if spec.get("model") else {}),
   167	            }
   168	        )
   169	    return {
   170	        "feature_slug": slug,
   171	        "stage": stage,
   172	        "artifact_path": repo_relative_path(artifact_path, REPO_ROOT),
   173	        "git_base_ref": base_ref or "",
   174	        "allowed_dirty_paths": list(allow_dirty_paths or []),
   175	        "required_reviews": manifest_reviews,
   176	        "max_artifact_chars": max_artifact_chars,
   177	        "max_context_chars": max_context_chars,
   178	        "max_total_chars": max_total_chars,
   179	    }
   180	
   181	
   182	def repair_checkpoint_args(slug: str, stage: str, state: dict[str, object]) -> argparse.Namespace:
   183	    manifest = load_checkpoint_manifest(slug, stage) or {}
   184	    workflow_state = load_workflow_state(slug)
   185	    context_paths: list[str] = []
   186	    for review in manifest.get("required_reviews", []):
   187	        for context_path in review.get("context_paths", []):
   188	            if context_path not in context_paths:
   189	                context_paths.append(context_path)
   190	    allow_dirty_paths = list(dict.fromkeys(manifest.get("allowed_dirty_paths", [])))

   184	                ng.append(args.non_goal)
   185	        if getattr(args, "acceptance_criteria", None) is not None:
   186	            ac = discovery.setdefault("acceptance_criteria", [])
   187	            if args.acceptance_criteria not in ac:
   188	                ac.append(args.acceptance_criteria)
   189	        blocking = blocking_unresolved_items(discovery)
   190	        if args.complete:
   191	            if blocking:
   192	                if discovery_blockers_are_malformed(discovery):
   193	                    raise SystemExit(
   194	                        "discover cannot mark discovery complete while discovery state is malformed; "
   195	                        "use discover --clear to reset malformed discovery state"
   196	                    )
   197	                raise SystemExit(
   198	                    "discover cannot mark discovery complete while unresolved items remain; "
   199	                    "resolve or defer each item first"
   200	                )
   201	            if not force_complete and int(discovery.get("asked_count", 0)) < int(discovery.get("question_count", 0)):
   202	                raise SystemExit(
   203	                    "discover cannot mark discovery complete before the planned questions are recorded; "
   204	                    "use --force-complete if you intentionally want to override the count"
   205	                )
   206	            discovery["complete"] = True
   207	        elif (
   208	            args.required
   209	            or args.count is not None
   210	            or args.question
   211	            or args.assumption
   212	            or args.summary is not None
   213	            or getattr(args, "answer", None) is not None
   214	            or getattr(args, "unresolved", None) is not None
   215	            or getattr(args, "resolve", None) is not None
   216	            or getattr(args, "defer", None) is not None
   217	            or getattr(args, "non_goal", None) is not None
   218	            or getattr(args, "acceptance_criteria", None) is not None
   219	        ):
   220	            discovery["complete"] = False
   221	        if force_complete:
   222	            if blocking:
   223	                raise SystemExit(
   224	                    "discover cannot force discovery complete while unresolved items remain; "
   225	                    "resolve or defer each item first"
   226	                )
   227	            discovery["complete"] = True
   228	        discovery["updated_at"] = int(time.time())
   229	
   230	    state = update_discovery_state(args.slug, mutate)
   231	    discovery = state.get(DISCOVERY_KEY, {})
   232	    remaining = max(int(discovery.get("question_count", 0)) - int(discovery.get("asked_count", 0)), 0)
   233	    print(f"workflow: {args.slug}")
   234	    print("discovery:")
   235	    print(f"- version: {discovery.get('version', 1)}")
   236	    print(f"- required: {'yes' if discovery.get('required') else 'no'}")
   237	    print(f"- complete: {'yes' if discovery.get('complete') else 'no'}")
   238	    print(f"- question-count: {discovery.get('question_count', 0)}")
   239	    print(f"- asked-count: {discovery.get('asked_count', 0)}")
   240	    print(f"- remaining: {remaining}")

   462	
   463	def _validate_verdict(verdict: dict) -> str | None:
   464	    required = ["judge", "model", "verdict", "confidence", "reasoning", "evidence", "timestamp"]
   465	    for key in required:
   466	        if key not in verdict:
   467	            return f"missing required field: {key}"
   468	    if verdict["judge"] not in VALID_LENSES:
   469	        return f"invalid judge: {verdict['judge']!r}"
   470	    if not isinstance(verdict["model"], str) or not verdict["model"].strip():
   471	        return "model must be a non-empty string"
   472	    if verdict["verdict"] not in {"proceed", "proceed-with-annotation", "block"}:
   473	        return f"invalid verdict: {verdict['verdict']!r}"
   474	    if not isinstance(verdict["confidence"], int) or not 0 <= verdict["confidence"] <= 5:
   475	        return "confidence must be an integer in the range 0..5"
   476	    if not isinstance(verdict["reasoning"], str) or len(verdict["reasoning"].strip()) < 10:
   477	        return "reasoning must be a string of at least 10 characters"
   478	    if "unaddressed_high_finding_ids" in verdict:
   479	        if not isinstance(verdict["unaddressed_high_finding_ids"], list):
   480	            return "unaddressed_high_finding_ids must be a list"
   481	        for item in verdict["unaddressed_high_finding_ids"]:
   482	            if not isinstance(item, str) or not item.strip():
   483	                return "unaddressed_high_finding_ids items must be non-empty strings"
   484	    if not isinstance(verdict["evidence"], list):
   485	        return "evidence must be a list"
   486	    for item in verdict["evidence"]:
   487	        if not isinstance(item, dict):
   488	            return "evidence items must be objects"
   489	        for key in ("artifact", "section", "quote"):
   490	            if key not in item or not isinstance(item[key], str):
   491	                return f"evidence item missing string field: {key}"
   492	    if not isinstance(verdict["timestamp"], str) or not verdict["timestamp"].strip():
   493	        return "timestamp must be a non-empty string"
   494	    # Tolerate harmless JSON-Schema metadata fields that judges sometimes
   495	    # echo back when the prompt includes the full schema (Claude in particular
   496	    # has been observed emitting `$schema` and `$id` alongside valid verdicts).
   497	    # These have no semantic meaning for the vote, so stripping them silently
   498	    # is correct and avoids false-block schema_violation fallbacks.
   499	    IGNORABLE_METADATA_FIELDS = {"$schema", "$id", "$comment", "title", "description"}
   500	    for meta_field in IGNORABLE_METADATA_FIELDS & set(verdict):
   501	        verdict.pop(meta_field, None)
   502	    extra = set(verdict) - set(required) - {"unaddressed_high_finding_ids"}
   503	    if extra:
   504	        return f"unexpected fields in verdict: {sorted(extra)}"
   505	    return None
   506

   514	    fallbacks purely because of fence wrapping; the actual JSON content was
   515	    valid and substantive.
   516	    """
   517	    if not raw:
   518	        return raw
   519	    text = raw.strip()

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import argparse
import hashlib
import json
import subprocess
import sys
from pathlib import Path


SCRIPT_DIR = Path(__file__).resolve().parent
RUN_GEMINI = SCRIPT_DIR / "run_gemini_review.py"
RUN_CODEX = SCRIPT_DIR / "run_codex_review.py"
VERIFY = SCRIPT_DIR / "verify_review_checkpoint.py"
if str(SCRIPT_DIR) not in sys.path:
    sys.path.insert(0, str(SCRIPT_DIR))

from workflow_utils import normalized_artifact_hash, normalized_artifact_text, resolve_stored_path

REPO_ROOT = SCRIPT_DIR.parents[5]
REPAIR_LIMIT_BUFFER_CHARS = 1000
REPAIR_MIN_TOTAL_BUFFER_CHARS = 10000


def sha256_file(path: Path) -> str:
    return hashlib.sha256(path.read_bytes()).hexdigest()


def parse_frontmatter(path: Path) -> tuple[dict[str, str], str]:
    text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
    if not text.startswith("---\n"):
        raise ValueError(f"{path} is missing frontmatter")
    _, rest = text.split("---\n", 1)
    fm_text, body = rest.split("\n---\n", 1)
    data: dict[str, str] = {}
    for line in fm_text.splitlines():
        if not line.strip():
            continue
        key, value = line.split(":", 1)
        data[key.strip()] = value.strip().strip('"')
    return data, body


def review_is_healthy(spec: dict, artifact_path: Path) -> bool:
    review_path = resolve_stored_path(spec["path"], REPO_ROOT)
    if not review_path.exists():
        return False
    try:
        data, body = parse_frontmatter(review_path)
    except Exception:
        return False
    recorded_artifact = resolve_stored_path(data.get("artifact_path", ""), REPO_ROOT, data.get("repo_root", ""))
    if recorded_artifact != artifact_path:
        return False
    if data.get("artifact_sha256") != normalized_artifact_hash(spec.get("stage", ""), artifact_path):
        return False
    if data.get("resolution_status") == "failed":
        return False
    if data.get("coverage_status") == "partial":
        return False
    for marker in ("# Review:", "## Findings", "## Residual Risks", "## Resolution"):
        if marker not in body:
            return False
    if data.get("reviewer") == "gemini":
        raw_output = data.get("raw_output_path", "")
        if not raw_output or not resolve_stored_path(raw_output, REPO_ROOT, data.get("repo_root", "")).exists():
            return False
    return True


def partial_coverage_reason(spec: dict) -> str:
    review_path = resolve_stored_path(spec["path"], REPO_ROOT)
    if not review_path.exists():
        return ""
    try:
        data, _ = parse_frontmatter(review_path)
    except Exception:
        return ""
    if data.get("coverage_status") != "partial":
        return ""
    return data.get("coverage_note", "")


def context_chars(spec: dict) -> int:
    total = 0
    for raw_path in spec.get("context_paths", []):
        path = resolve_stored_path(raw_path, REPO_ROOT)
        if path.exists():
            total += len(path.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
    return total


def expanded_checkpoint_for_partial_artifact(spec: dict, artifact_path: Path, checkpoint: dict) -> dict | None:
    if "artifact exceeded max_artifact_chars" not in partial_coverage_reason(spec):
        return None

    artifact_chars = len(normalized_artifact_text(checkpoint["stage"], artifact_path))
    expanded = dict(checkpoint)
    expanded["max_artifact_chars"] = max(
        int(checkpoint.get("max_artifact_chars") or 0),
        artifact_chars + REPAIR_LIMIT_BUFFER_CHARS,
    )
    expanded["max_total_chars"] = max(
        int(checkpoint.get("max_total_chars") or 0),
        expanded["max_artifact_chars"] + context_chars(spec) + REPAIR_MIN_TOTAL_BUFFER_CHARS,
    )
    return expanded


def run_gemini(
    spec: dict,
    artifact_path: Path,
    checkpoint: dict,
    workspace_dir: Path | None,
    timeout_seconds: int,
    retries: int,
) -> None:
    cmd = [
        sys.executable,
        str(RUN_GEMINI),
        "--artifact",
        str(artifact_path),
        "--lens",
        spec["lens"],
        "--stage",
        checkpoint["stage"],
        "--output",
        spec["path"],
    ]
    for context_path in spec.get("context_paths", []):
        cmd.extend(["--context", context_path])
    if checkpoint.get("git_base_ref"):
        cmd.extend(["--git-base-ref", checkpoint["git_base_ref"]])
    if spec.get("model"):
        cmd.extend(["--model", spec["model"]])
    if checkpoint.get("max_artifact_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-artifact-chars", str(checkpoint["max_artifact_chars"])])
    if checkpoint.get("max_context_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-context-chars", str(checkpoint["max_context_chars"])])
    if checkpoint.get("max_total_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-total-chars", str(checkpoint["max_total_chars"])])
    if workspace_dir:
        cmd.extend(["--workspace-dir", str(workspace_dir)])
    cmd.extend(["--timeout-seconds", str(timeout_seconds), "--retries", str(retries)])
    subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, text=True, timeout=timeout_seconds + 30)


def run_codex(
    spec: dict,
    artifact_path: Path,
    checkpoint: dict,
    workspace_dir: Path | None,
) -> None:
    cmd = [
        sys.executable,
        str(RUN_CODEX),
        "--artifact",
        str(artifact_path),
        "--lens",
        spec["lens"],
        "--stage",
        checkpoint["stage"],
        "--output",
        spec["path"],
    ]
    for context_path in spec.get("context_paths", []):
        cmd.extend(["--context", context_path])
    if checkpoint.get("git_base_ref"):
        cmd.extend(["--git-base-ref", checkpoint["git_base_ref"]])
    if spec.get("model"):
        cmd.extend(["--model", spec["model"]])
    if checkpoint.get("max_artifact_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-artifact-chars", str(checkpoint["max_artifact_chars"])])
    if checkpoint.get("max_context_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-context-chars", str(checkpoint["max_context_chars"])])
    if checkpoint.get("max_total_chars"):
        cmd.extend(["--max-total-chars", str(checkpoint["max_total_chars"])])
    if workspace_dir:
        cmd.extend(["--workspace-dir", str(workspace_dir)])
    subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, text=True, timeout=210)


def main() -> int:
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    parser.add_argument("--checkpoint-manifest", required=True)
    parser.add_argument("--workspace-dir")
    parser.add_argument("--gemini-timeout-seconds", type=int, default=120)
    parser.add_argument("--gemini-retries", type=int, default=1)
    args = parser.parse_args()

    manifest_path = Path(args.checkpoint_manifest).resolve()
    checkpoint = json.loads(manifest_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
    artifact_path = resolve_stored_path(checkpoint["artifact_path"], REPO_ROOT)
    workspace_dir = Path(args.workspace_dir).resolve() if args.workspace_dir else None

    failed_codex: list[str] = []
    failed_gemini: list[str] = []
    for spec in checkpoint.get("required_reviews", []):
        if review_is_healthy(spec, artifact_path):
            continue
        review_checkpoint = expanded_checkpoint_for_partial_artifact(spec, artifact_path, checkpoint)
        if review_checkpoint:
            print(
                f"repair expanding artifact budget for {spec['path']} to "
                f"{review_checkpoint['max_artifact_chars']} chars",
                file=sys.stderr,
            )
        else:
            review_checkpoint = checkpoint
        if spec.get("reviewer") == "gemini":
            try:
                run_gemini(
                    spec,
                    artifact_path,
                    review_checkpoint,
                    workspace_dir,
                    args.gemini_timeout_seconds,
                    args.gemini_retries,
                )
            except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:
                failed_gemini.append(f"{spec['path']} (repair timeout)")

## Findings
- **High** [CODE-CONFIRMED]: `--validation-only` is underspecified against the current manifest format. The spec says to “re-seal the manifest” and update an `artifact_sha256` field ([spec.md:49](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/feature-runs/ff-quality-of-life/spec.md#L49), [spec.md:148](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/feature-runs/ff-quality-of-life/spec.md#L148)), but `checkpoint_manifest()` does not store any SHA at all ([factory_review.py:144](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/feature-factory/scripts/factory_review.py#L144)), and the verifier only checks review-file frontmatter `artifact_sha256` against the artifact hash ([verify_review_checkpoint.py:149](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/review-lens/scripts/verify_review_checkpoint.py#L149), [verify_review_checkpoint.py:173](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/review-lens/scripts/verify_review_checkpoint.py#L173)). As written, the spec needs a manifest schema change it never calls out.

- **Medium** [CODE-CONFIRMED]: The budget “raise” is not a pure raise. The proposed defaults are `40000 / 50000 / 200000` in the spec ([spec.md:136](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/feature-runs/ff-quality-of-life/spec.md#L136)), but the downstream review runners already default to `50000 / 10000 / 70000` ([run_codex_review.py:51](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/review-lens/scripts/run_codex_review.py#L51), [run_gemini_review.py:484](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/review-lens/scripts/run_gemini_review.py#L484)). Lowering the artifact cap to 40k can make artifact-heavy runs narrow earlier than they do today, so this can reintroduce partial coverage on cases that currently fit.

- **Medium** [CODE-CONFIRMED]: The restatement hardening is still prompt-only and not actually enforced by the runner. The spec asks for a test that fails schema validation when a severity-drop rationale lacks quotes ([spec.md:106](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/feature-runs/ff-quality-of-life/spec.md#L106)), but `run_judge()` only checks JSON shape and field presence in `_validate_verdict()` ([factory_cmd_judge.py:463](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/feature-factory/scripts/factory_cmd_judge.py#L463)). The prompt already tells the model to quote specific text from old and new rounds ([restatement.md:49](/Users/chrislaw/valuerank/.claude/worktrees/friendly-aryabhata-9efbf7/docs/workflow/operations/codex-skills/feature-factory/judge-prompts/restatement.md#L49)), so this spec does not add a machine-checkable guard.

## Residual Risks
- `--validation-only` still needs a precise rule for which review files it rewrites if the manifest lists multiple reviews for a stage. The manifest only names `required_reviews`; it does not carry a separate source of truth for which files are safe to reseal.

- `discover` append semantics will still depend on exact-string deduplication. Near-duplicates that differ only by whitespace or casing can still accumulate unless the spec also defines normalization.

- The restatement fix will still depend on model compliance unless you add a post-parse validator or a structured field. Prompt text alone can reduce risk, but it cannot guarantee behavior.
